<Author>md9802
<Content>Loved Hotel Fita! I highly recommend Fita to everyone. I stayed there for a night in October while on vacation. I knew I would be arriving at the hotel at 10A, a few hours before regular check-in time. Much to my surprise, my room was ready for me when I arrived. Loes graciously welcomed me into the hotel. The single room was small but clean. It had everything I needed. My room was on the first floor but there was an elevator as noted but many other reviews. Since I was leaving early the next morning, Loes even took my laundry (free!) when I checked in so that it would be ready later the same day.Loes was extremely helpful with directions, pointing out the relevant buses/trams and good restaurants in the area. The hotel is located on a quiet street, just around the corner from the Museumplein. It's also within walking distance of Vondelpark and the nightlife of Leidseplein. There is a free computer with internet access and a printer - great for printing out your boarding pass before heading to the airport. There is also free wireless available in the rooms. Breakfast was hearty and filling - yogurt, eggs, croissants, and fruit. Even stroopwafels! Local calls and even calls to the US are free, which was fantastic. Both Hans and Loes were warm, welcoming hosts that made me feel at home. I would readily stay at Fita again on my next trip to Amsterdam.

<Author>WmCT
<Content>Great little hotel in quiet neighborhood Most of the reviews describe the property well. It's in a good location for the Van Gogh and Rijksmuseum....just a stone's throw away. Very nice people who run it - very friendly and helpful. Room was small, but that's typical for Europe, but clean and very cozy. Flat screen TV and wireless - very important for me. The bath room had it's own radiator and so was always very toasty warm. The ONLY possible negative could be that the hotel is located very near a day-care, so often you could hear screaming children during the day. It didn't really bother me, but I just thought I'd mention it. Breakfast was good - typical European, and they offered to custom cook eggs if I wanted. Just an all-around good place with a good price. I paid 100 Euro, and that's cheap for Amsterdam.

<Author>HinghamVirginia
<Content>Loved Hotel Fita! Amsterdam was our last stop before returning to the states. My husband and I were traveling with our 4 children ranging in ages from 13 to 23. We had spent 2 days in Paris and 2 days in Normandy before checking into Hotel Fita. It was like coming home. We arrived very late in the evening and Hans, the owner, couldn't have been more welcoming and hospitable. We were exhausted and to have two very large rooms that were spotless, warm and comfy was awesome! It is a non-smoking hotel which we really appreciated! The bathrooms were large and spotlessly clean. Upon our arrival that evening, Hans couldn't have been nicer. He has a great sense of humor and my kids just loved him. He told us about the amenities the hotel offers including the free internet service (kids immediately disappeared), gave us our room keys, cards to enter after hours, put our luggage on the lift, and showed us to our rooms. The next morning, we followed the wonderful aroma of coffee, eggs and bacon down the stairs to the cozy dining room where we were greeted by a jovial Hans and served a delicious buffet breakfast. There was a wonderful assortment of cheeses and Hans' homemade jams. Delicious! We asked Hans to help us plan our short stay and he gave us an itinerary to follow sending us through the little streets of the city to some of the prettiest places including gardens, canal overlooks, and the flower market. Hans then suggested we stop at a wonderful cheese shop and then continue on and get a beer at the Papeneiland Pub. This is one of the oldest establishments in Amsterdam and was the perfect stop before continuing on with our day. We walked to the Anne Frank House and finished up at the Van Gogh Museum before returning to Hotel Fita which was just a short walk from the museum. With such a short stay in the city, the Hotel Fita and Hans were the perfect choice for us. We all cannot wait to return for a longer stay in Amsterdam at the Hotel Fita!!! Thank you Hans and Loes!

<Author>Gilmann
<Content>Great stay I spent a lot of time researching Amsterdam hotels before my trip and chose Hotel Fita due to other reviews, and thought I'd add a bit.It's incredibly close to Museumplein, so if you plan to visit the Rijksmuseum or Van Gogh, it's hard to get closer. It's a 5 minute walk to restaurants, or a 15-20 minute walk to the center of town (and being Amsterdam, it's a fun walk).Hotel is clean, paint is fresh. Beds are small but comfortable. Rooms are as stated (when you reserve, you choose the room size); ours was roomy enough for two leisure/business travellers carrying multiple large suitcases. Free wireless internet. We were welcomed with champagne by the owner, it was a nice touch after a long travel day.Above the norm: the hotel has a lift, and as I've stayed at BB's in Amsterdam that don't I can assure this was a big, big plus. The breakfast was excellent: freshly brewed coffee, scrambled eggs  crisp bacon, freshly squeezed orange juice, pastries, cheeses, etc. Very nice breakfast area.Booked through Hoteliers.com. Booking process is not a highlight, it took a couple of emails and calls to get it done, but it worked in the end.Highly recommend.

<Content>Pleasant stay We stayed in a twin room at Fita Hotel in early september for 3 nights, after a few days in London, where we stayed in a chain hotel. We found this hotel very nice for many reasons. First, the location. We enjoyed walking to Leidsplein every day either to eat, sightseeing or shopping. Second, the room. This things might be not important for a lot of people, but it were for us as we needed to keep in touch with our family and arrange tickets and accomodation for the rest of our trip. The owners provided good information about the city and also gave a warm welcome. It was very convenient to buy tickets for the museum from them and avoid the HUGE line in Van Gogh Museum.

<Content>Best kept secret in Amsterdam This is the first time I have ever written a review for ANYTHING online so trust me when I say that you will be thoroughly impressed with your stay at Hotel Fita. I stumbled upon this hotel while searching for a comfortable, quaint and reasonably priced place to stay during my trip to Amsterdam. I highly, HIGHLY recommend this hotel to anyone who wants a lovely place to stay that is within walking distance to so many local treasures and hot spots. I will never stay anywhere but here during my future visits to Amsterdam.

<Content>Very nice stay. Would recommend My wife and I stayed at Hotel Fita for three nights. As many have said, the hotel is in an excellent location and many sights are within walking distance. Our room was on the ground floor and was very spacious. We found our room clean and tidy and the owners very hospitable.We thought Hans had a very good breakfast, although the oranges do run out if you're the last down in the morning. We found both Hans and Loes very friendly and easy to talk to. Hans makes it a point to talk to everyone when they come for breakfast. Loes suggested some very nice restaurants in the area and we enjoyed talking with her and her daughter. Unlike other posts here, we found Loes very friendly and a real treat to talk to!The only negative we experienced was with the maid service. We put the 'Do Not Disturb' sign on the door (we don't like having maids come in our room for short stays) and found that when we came back, the maid had been in and made up the room. We thought that maybe we had forgotten to put the placard up, but the following day she again came into the room. We asked her not to clean our room, but she didn't seem to understand. It was our last night, so we didn't bother saying anything to Hans.We would stay here again, and would recommend this to our friends.

<Author>makamaCalifornia
<Content>Loved Hotel Fita My husband and I had one of the large rooms with a little sitting area that looks out over the schoolyard across the street.We had a king-size bed with two twin-sized duvets beneath a king-size bedspread--not standard U.S. practice. But based on our experiences during the previous two weeks driving around Germany and Switzerland, putting two twin-sized duvets on a double bed was standard at all the BBs we stayed at. This was also the case in the private home of our German host couple.We felt that the room was always well cleaned. During a 6-day stay, the only comment we would make is that it took two days for wine glasses to be removed from the room. Now, you should also know how the wine glasses got there: One of the staff members brought us wine and nuts on our first night because we arrived late in the evening like basket cases after a six-hour drive from Germany that should have taken three hours. Adriaan took great pity on us and brought up that little treat, which was so, so welcome.We met the owner and, as a very hearty Dutchman, he can definitely seem a bit larger than life. But he was perfectly pleasant and very helpful. Now let me tell you more wonderful things about Hotel Fita: a friendly staff that is there to please you; free use of a computer for Internet access just outside the breakfast room; free--yes, free--laundry service (can you imagine how wonderful that was for us after traveling for two weeks?); a lovely buffet breakfast; steps from the Rijksmuseum and the Van Gogh Museum, and well-located for walking anywhere in the Centrum; and a resident wire-haired dachshund named Bella who will cheer all guests who are missing their pups at home.In our opinion, you can't go wrong with Hotel Fita.

<Author>madmadeleine
<Content>Hotel Owners have FITS at Hotel Fita I had a problem at this hotel. The husband and wife team that run this hotel seem like nice people, but try to complain, and they go on the attack, and they are vicious and relentless. Be warned. I expect to be harassed because I am posting this review. The following is a true account of what happened to me.After kicking us out two days in a row to clean our room, the maid had yet to remove the dirty glassware or clean the room properly. The mirror in the bathroom had tooth flossing specks on it, not from us. There was mildew on the grout in the bathtub. The glass topped coffee table had grease on both sides of the glass and the rug and not been vacuumed. The windows on the french doors were dirty on both sides--these windows were easily accessible, and oddly, the other windows in the window seat area, which were harder to get at, were clean. The room was actually very nice, one of the best in the hotel. And with 10 minutes and some windex and bleach, all would have been fine.However, when I tried to explain this to Hans, one of the owners of the hotel, he went ballistic. I was not aware that complaining was not permitted in their hotel.While we were alone in my room, this intimidating man became irate. He yelled at me for being too demanding! I told him maybe he was unaware that the maid wasn't taking care of all the details when cleaning even though she made such a point of kicking us out of our room for her to clean it.The first day we were there. We were so jet lagged we went back to bed and were fast asleep when the maid walked in on us! We had put the do not disturb sign on the door, but she said it had fallen on the floor. She didn't even knock! She insisted that she had to clean the room immediately and gave us 10 minutes to dress and get out. We were too groggy to stand up for ourselves, or to complain about such treatment. The next day, my husband had left to work at the trade show but I was still in the room when she came in and wanted to clean it. So I grabbed my stuff and got out.When I got back I noticed she made the bed and changed the towels. I went downstairs to get some ice and since the ice bucket that had been in our room was not clean, I went into the kitchen and washed it in the sink with some dish soap. I was approached by one of the other employees who asked what I was doing. I told her that the ice bucket had not been clean and I wanted to wash it before putting ice in it. I told her things in our room were not as clean as I would have hoped they would be.A few minutes later, Hans came up with windex and bleach. He said something about that he had told the maid to bleach the mildew in the tub, and he went in to do that. I took the windex and started to do the bathroom mirror and he went ballistic. I pointed out the toothpaste spray on the mirror and said that it had been there since we arrived, and suggested that he might have a problem with his maid not doing her job properly. And we didn't appreciate her walking in on us or kicking us out of our room when we had obviously been asleep! Hans started shouting at me about how unreasonably picky I was being and that everything can't be perfect in a room. He then ran his hand over the top of the armoire and it came down covered with dust! I had no idea what his point was, I wasn't even complaining about the dust, but it was comic how he was raging defensively about how clean the room was and it was actually even dirtier than I had noticed.About a half hour later I was having trouble using the wireless internet, so I went downstairs to try the set-up they have for the guests that don't have laptops, and I saw some windex and a towel next to the computer. So I borrowed these items and took the opportunity to clean the stuff that had been bothering me. I replaced the items when I was done.I sent an email to Loes, who was my initial contact when I booked my stay. She is the wife of Hans and from what I can tell, a co-owner. I told her This is not acceptable behavior. I would like someone to apologize to me in a civil manner and I expect polite treatment and good service for the remainder of my stay. Then she called to shout at me and tell me how happy she is with all of her staff. And since I did not like my room, I could move out immediately! Now she was being spiteful. With the one of the biggest trade shows of the year in town, there was no way I was going to be able to find anything, and I was not the one that was unable to control my temper. I told her I would see what I could do. And I told her that since I had had a chance to clean the room, it was satisfactory. But that only made her angrier. She came to my door and pounded on it! I told her I was not going to open the door or participate in a shouting match. I told her if she could find a comparable room at another hotel, I would move. She tried, but couldn't come up with anything. So I was stuck wondering everytime I went out whether my stuff was safe in a place where they were so rude and wanted to get me out so badly. And worrying every time I came in that I would see Hans or Loes and they would yell at me again. They got to save some money, because we did not go down to breakfast. We ate out rather than risk any confrontation. That's okay. Hans rules over the breakfast room and our first morning we must have come down later than he wished, even though it was still within the allotted breakfast time. So there was no fresh squeezed orange juice for us! I went online to trip advisor and sorted by one star reviews. I found multiple complaints about them bullying their customers! Guess I should have done more research... To prevent more confrontations, I sent her an email telling her that since she and Hans could not seem to control their tempers, that the only way I would communicate with them was by email. And that they both owed me an apology. There was no apology, and though we had scheduled more days after the trade show, we got out of there as soon as we could.One more little annoyance. We paid extra to get the largest room size because it featured a double bed that was a real double bed, not two singles stuck together. But the bed was topped by two small (probably single size) duvet-like things instead of one that fit the bed. The overlap was pretty small, so In the middle of the night, they would slip around on the bed and create a gap right where we were trying to sleep together. They topped it with a thin chenille bedspread that was the right size, so things looked okay on the surface.It's a shame. It is a nice hotel with a lot of great perks. But the inability of the management to control their negative emotions makes it intolerable. Amsterdam has lots of wonderful places to stay. This is not one of them.

<Author>TravelLoverBoston
<Content>Hotel Fita is Number One in Amsterdam!! I spent 3 days in Amsterdam before embarking on a cruise in August, 2008. Based on TripAdvisor reviews, I booked a single room for myself and for my travel companion...and I cannot think of a single reason why anyone would stay anywhere else. The location in the Museum Quarter is excellent. A very quiet street that is near just about anything you may want to do, PLUS the city is very walkable. The hotel itself is spotlessly clean and has one of the friendliest, most helpful, will-do-anything-for-you staffs that I have ever seen. My single room was a perfect size (and keep in mind that I had clothing for a 2 week trip to store), the bathrooms are fantastic (great shower!), plus I had a balcony!! Breakfast is first rate and changes daily. The coffee and food and juice were all delicious. If I am ever lucky enough to visit Amsterdam again I will stay at the Hotel Fita!!

<Author>CCinLouisiana
<Content>Loved the Fita Hotel Fita is a nice, small hotel in a great location. It is near the Rembrandt museum and Rijksmuseum, near tram and bus stops, and in a residential area so visitors may get a glimpse of how Amsterdam residents live, commute to work on bicycles and bring their children to school. Entrance to the hotel is restricted, which makes one feel safe. The room was lovely. I had a balcony overlooking a school playground. The bathroom was large, with a shower and bathtub (and rubber duck!) You can buy tickets to the Rembrandt Museum and Rijksmuseum through the hotel. The breakfast was good. The breakfast room was set up so that visitors could easily converse and make acquaintances. It was a lovely place, a great location. I would stay there again!

<Author>54austin
<Content>Great location, modest accommodations Hotel Fita is a clean, modest, little hotel in a great location. On a quiet residential street, it's a short block away from both the Van Gogh Museum and Amsterdam's Fifth Avenue. It's far enough away from the riff-raff of the old city center that you don't feel like you're trapped in tourist hell, but near enough (and Amsterdam's so compact, anyway), that it's all easily accessible by foot. It's also close to Amsterdam's largest park and several supermarkets, which makes for an easy economical picnic.The rooms are clean, but these are very much standard 3-star standards. There are some nice touches, such as a free use of an espresso maker in the room, cable TV, hot breakfast, internet, and a welcome glass of champagne and nuts. Staff are also generally friendly and helpful. But if you look around for specials at some of the other 4/5-star hotels in town, you could probably find a room at the same rate. It's this place's reliability, location and cleanliness keep it a consistent favorite.

<Author>RVS798
<Content>Friendly and forgiving We had a reservation to spend four nights at the Hotel Fita, but our flight from Istanbul was delayed, then canceled -- so I had to call at the last minute and tell the hotel we'd be arriving the next day and would be spending only three nights. Although they would have had every right, under their written policy, to charge us for the first night, they didn't -- which tells you all you need to know about the friendliness and hospitality of this delightful boutique hotel. We splurged for the largest room (165 Euros) and believe me it was worth it! After years of suffering postage stamp-sized hotel rooms in Europe, this was a real treat -- and being less than a block away from the Van Gogh Museum on a lovely, quiet, residential street was an added bonus. Highly recommended.

<Author>Sandydeepbay
<Content>A jewel in Amsterdam We arrived at the Hotel Fita at the end of our three week trip through France and Amsterdam. My husband, myself and my mother-in-law thought this was the most elegant hotel we had stayed in during our trip. Hans met us and showed us our rooms, where he left with us glasses of bubbly and a bowl of cashews. Our two rooms were on the same floor and we felt secure enough that during the times we were at the hotel, we could leave our doors open and walk down to my in-laws room to check on her. Our double room was very large, airy and immaculate. Our bathroom had amenities which we had never seen before in a hotel. PS. We loved the rubber duck! Our breakfasts were delicious and varied. And we appreciated the freshly squeezed orange juice every morning. We also appreciated the free computer next to the breakfast room to email our kids. Hotel Fita was located in a quiet, leafy neighbourhood. Very central to walk to the museums, restaurants and designer shops to admire the evening gowns. Unfortunately, my husband contracted a bug, and Hans brought him a tray of tea, honey and a lime. A very lovely gesture. Our time in Amsterdam was much to short. We would love to come back again to visit this beautiful city and country and we will definitely return to the Hotel Fita. Thank you Hans and Loes.

<Author>alself
<Content>Excellent deal on hotel in great location Hotel Fita is ideally situated for seeing the Van Gogh and Rijks museums - just a few steps away from each. It is also located within walking distance of many restaurants and other tourist shops. The rooms are nicely appointed with free wireless internet and free international calls to the US - an excellent perk for business travelers. The owners are very welcoming, offering a glass of champagne and cashews upon check-in as well as a wealth of advice of what to see and do while in town and how best to get there. They also arranged an early breakfast for me due to early departure. Lastly, the Airport Connexion hotel shuttle stops at Hotel Fita and provides excellent economy for travelers looking to get to the hotel without paying a premium taxi service. I couldn't have asked for more and plan to make Hotel Fita a regular stop on future trips through Amsterdam.

<Author>loulie44
<Content>Lovely hotel, centrally located My husband, 9-year-old son and I stayed at the Hotel Fita for four nights last week and had a wonderful experience. The hotel is on a quiet street that is centrally located. (It's right around the corner from the Van Gogh museum and Rijksmuseum, and a five minute walk to the Leidesplein, where we spent much time sitting on the terraces of various cafes.) We stayed in Room 32, which is one of the largest rooms and easily accommodated the extra bed they brought in for my son. The room has the added bonus of a balcony, where my husband and I enjoyed an evening glass of wine after my son fell asleep. The breakfast included in the room rate is tasty and included freshly baked croissants, raisin brioches, and chocolate croissants; bread and cheese; eggs and bacon; cereal; various fruits and orange juice; and freshly brewed coffee. The staff was pleasant and helpful, and the hotel is impeccably clean. My husband is a native of Amsterdam, and remarked that the hotel was the ideal combination of being in a peaceful location that is central to the sites. We give the hotel our highest recommendation.

<Author>Tatania77
<Content>Simply excellent My husband and I really loved this hotel. It was clean and it smelled clean, too. The location was very good and the staff were very helpful. The room we stayed in was spacious (not just by Amsterdam standards) and had a nice big bathroom, lovely big windows and a balcony. The view wasn't anything special, but the street is quiet at night, so if you value a good night's sleep more than an exciting view, this hotel is certainly a good choice. One of the best things is their buffet breakfast served in a pretty little room. We found ourselves rather looking forward to all those scrambled eggs, bacon, toast, pastries of all kinds, fruit salad...makes me hungry to be writing about it now!The only shortcoming was our bed which was two twin beds put together, but that is a common feature of most hotels in Amsterdam. Otherwise the bed was quite comfortable.We certainly felt very lucky to have chosen this hotel and would recommend it to anyone.

<Author>Genings
<Content>As good as the reviews say We won't repeat the details in the previous reviews, but will just say that they are all true: this is a wonderful little hotel, absolutely spotlessly clean. Fine breakfast buffet. The location is spectacular, and the nearby #2 and 5 streetcars will take you everywhere (7-8 minute ride to within 4 blocks of the Anne Frank House, for example); we never waited more than 5 minutes for one. The Van Gogh museum is 75 yards away, and the Concertgebouw three blocks. The staff is extremely helpful and friendly. One earlier review carped about the small elevator: yes, it's not large, but two people plus some luggage fit easily, and most hotels don't have an elevator at all. Among the other amenities: free laundry service. Just an outstanding value, all around.

<Author>Patmel
<Content>Hotel Fita - One of Amsterdam's Best Kept Secrets! The Hotel Fita is a small, friendly, family owned and run hotel. It is situated in a small residential road 50 yards from the Van Gogh Museum and tram stops and 100 yards from the Rijksmuseum. Vondel Park, the Leidesplein and the Concertgebrou are all within a few minutes walking distance.Booking over the hotel's website was quick and easy followed by a short 'phone call to Loes (the owner) to finalise a few points.We arrived at the hotel before the official booking-in time but were pleased to find out that our room was cleaned and ready. The room was bright and very, very clean and the large bathroom was spotless and with the radiator turned on - always a bonus for me!The room had several extras such as a room safe, coffee maker, ceiling fan and a welcome glass of wine each.Loes and her team were all very knowledgeable and helpful about places of interest, museums, travel arrangements etc. Nothing was too much trouble.Another point, as the owners actually live at the hotel, we felt particularly safe.We stayed at the Fita ten years ago and will certainly stop there again - but this time we won't leave it ten year!

<Content>We loved the Hotel Fita!! The Hotel Fita is a wonderful hotel that I highly recommend! It鈥檚 located in the Museum District, and you can walk to either the Rijksmuseum or the Van Gogh Museum in less than 5 minutes. I鈥檓 sure it鈥檚 not as centrally located as some might prefer, but we had no problem walking 鈥?or bicycling (fun!) 鈥?into the most central part of the city, up to Centraal station, and back again. And the beautiful, peaceful, tree-covered streets with quaint canals made me appreciate that we weren鈥檛 entirely in the thick of things. The hotel room itself was very pleasant 鈥?plenty large enough; we never felt like we were tripping over our luggage. The bathroom was *huge* and spotlessly clean. Just outside our door was a computer terminal with internet that any of the hotel鈥檚 guests could use for free, and down the hall, was the breakfast room. The breakfasts were quite nice 鈥?not terribly large or varied but still very good and much-appreciated, and the best part was the fresh-squeezed orange juice that the owner made for each guest. All of the hotel鈥檚 workers were extremely nice and eager to help in any way they could. Upon check-in, the front desk worker showed us the room and offered her assistance with anything we needed, then left, only to return several minutes later with 2 glasses of sparkling wine and a bowl of nuts to snack on. So, so very nice and thoughtful! The free laundry service was another perk. We just told someone we鈥檇 love to take advantage of that offer, expecting they鈥檇 tell us where to find the washer and dryer so we could wash our clothes, but instead, they told us to leave our clothes in a bag outside our door and they would be returned to us later that day, clean. We felt a bit badly, because we had about a week鈥檚 worth of laundry that needed to be done (we were in the middle of a month-long European vacation), but it couldn鈥檛 be helped, and after all, we *had* chosen to stay there 鈥?in part 鈥?specifically because of the laundry service. Oh, and I almost forgot one of the biggest perks: free phone calls to anywhere in the world! We loved having the chance to speak with our families, to let them know everything was going okay. So, in short: the free phone calls, free internet, and free laundry service were what made us pick Hotel Fita to begin with, but the location and friendliness of the staff, as well as the general comfort of the room/bathroom, were what pushed it onto our Extremely Highly Recommended list! Before coming to Amsterdam, I hadn't expected to fall in love with it. I was *excited* about our other destinations (London, Paris, Rome, Venice, Loire Valley) but just couldn't get 'pumped up' about Amsterdam. How wrong I was! I fell in complete and total love with this small, beautiful, and most of all friendly city, even preferring it over every other destination but my first-and-always love, Paris. <Author>dollySanFrancisco
<Content>great hotel My husband and I spent three comfortable nights at Hotel Fita this November, 2007. We were totally satisfied with all aspects. Our room, single deluxe, was large, perfectly clean, well appointed, and very comfortable. Closet space was most adequate. We very much appreciated the free access to the telephone for calls worldwide, as well as the free internet service. The staff was most friendly and helpful. Location is about as good as it gets. The Van Gogh Museum is less than a half block away as is the Reij Museum and the tram service. The area is quiet and has fabulous shopping and restaurant within minutes of a walk. We had the pleasure of meeting the proprietor of the hotel at breakfast one morning. We so very much enjoyed our chat with him and he gave us some excellent suggestions for dinners nearby. We hope to visit Amsterdam again, and will certainly make every effort to stay at Hotel Fita. Not to forget to mention that the plentiful and excellent breakfast is included in a very attractive room price. Perhaps, I should also mention that this is a small hotel (16 rooms) and that gives you a more intimate feeling, void of the impersonal feeling of the large hotel.

<Author>WidleyTraveller
<Content>Second visit to Hotel Fita and its still a great place to stay This was my second visit to Amsterdam and yet again to the Hotel Fita. I can certainly recommend it on all counts. The rooms are clean, well appointed and include a safe. Breakfasts are good and smell wonderful. The area is safe and one road away from the Amsterdam equivalent of Bond Street in London eg Pieter Cornelisz Hooft Straat (eg Cartier, Chanel etc). We ate at the nearby restaurants L'Entrecote et les dames (Van Baerlestraat) and the Hard Rock Cafe (Leidesplein). Sadly, the service from one older waitress at L'Entrecote et les dames was not very good and despite pre-booking a table for 9 she got very flustered and had to be calmed down by a younger staff member - otherwise the food was excellent.The Hotel Fita also has free phone calls to the UK  USA and wireless internet plus a internet point by the breakfast room - all free. The staff were incredibly helpful and I can certainly recommend it. Parking outside is generally possible but not cheap. Using a nearby car park such as 'Byzantine' by Leidesplein would be my recommendation but this time we had a minibus that wouldn't fit under the barrier!!When I next stay in Amsterdam it will definitely be at the Hotel Fita.

<Author>SuperDosa
<Content>Will recommend it. We stayed here for one night as part of a quick weekend trip to Amsterdam, and used Tripadvisor to narrow down choosing a hotel from the 100's available. Overall, was happy with the hotel. Positives were that it was very very clean, polite and helpful staff, nice location close to the Van Gogh Museum (they gave us discounted tickets as well), free breakfast included which was good and free international calls (really). Also had a free computer with an internet connection which allowed us to check in online for our flight. Only negatives are as follows and are minor - 1) our room was on the lower floor and while initially I was worried of being to close to the street etc, it wasnt that noisy the next morning...perhaps as it was a sunday. 2) In the bathroom, instead of providing hand soaps they had a liquid soap dispenser which wasnt that good (will recommend taking your own soap). The shower pressure was excellent though. Please note that as we were here for only one night we had different expectations as we werent planning on staying in the hotel all that much and wanted to walk around taking in all the sights - we were very content with the time we did though including sleeping. Will recommend it to friends.

<Author>peanutsrio
<Content>Very disappointed with room and bed Although we agree that this is a very well located hotel, with clean rooms and free laundry service, my wife and I were very disappointed with our stay. In our opinion it is very overrated and what we got was not what we expected based on the information on the site. We booked this hotel for 4 nights because of the reviews, hoping for something special and what we encountered was not at all what we expected. We booked the double deluxe room based on the image on the website - only to be told when we arrived that not all the deluxe rooms have a veranda, they are only deluxe because of size. The onwer couldn`t move us to one with a veranda, and admitted that the image on the website had led to this sort of problem before, and said he was going to change it.. One month later, the image remains the same.We were also diappointed with the bed. From the images, the other rooms clearly have two singles made up together, but the deluxe one looks like a double bed - but our room had 2 single beds made up separately and pushed togerther. Not what you expect at 160 euros a night! We think that the veranda and bed issue should have been clarified with us in the email communications before we finalised the booking. We certainly would not have booked the deluxe room if we had known. Lesson learnt: confirm every detail before finalising a booking - don't rely on the information/images on the website.One other thing, both my wife and I found the beds terrible for our backs - we both found them uncomfortable and left us with back pains in the morning. As soon as we went on to the next city and different accomodation these back problems went away.Apart from the very friendly girl who gave us a lot of information when we arrived , it was not easy to get advice about museums, trips etc, as reception was always empty and you had to speak to the owner on the telephone - but he seemed a little impatient and we found we got better help from the internet. It was useful having access to a computer on the internet, and also one other good thing was that local calls from thehotel room were free.We returned to Amsterdam a week later for 2 nights before flying back to Brazil and this time stayed 2 nights in Hotel Ibis and a much cheaper rate, and had a lovely double bed, which was good for our backs, and we wished we had stayed the other nights there. The tram service is very good for getting to the museums etc. We will not be staying in Hotel Fita again when we return to Amsterdam - and return we will, because it is a beautiful city.

<Content>Loved The Hotel Fita My husband and I just returned from a three week vacation in Europe and had the pleasure of staying one week at the wonderful Hotel Fita in Amsterdam. We absolutely loved the Hotel Fita in Amsterdam and will definitely stay there again on our next trip to Amsterdam. <Author>bigbertha707
<Content>The Right way, the Dutch way One thing to keep in mind about the Dutch is that if you are ever invited into the home of a Dutch person, than this is usually considered a very special thing. I was taught that this kind of invitation means you are considered a friend, and friendship is usually not taken lightly with the Dutch. It is typically a long process. At Hotel Fita, i felt as though i was invited into a Dutch home and treated as a friend. And in reality, you are coming into the home of the owners Hans and Loes de Rapper. They own and run the hotel. The hotel was very clean and quite spacious considering it is a renovated large house. The hotel is located in the perfect position, only a hop away from the Van Gogh Museum. When greeted by Loes, she was very quick to give us a map and outline the major points of the city. And even though i had already been to Amsterdam 5 times, she introduced me to something new that i had never done before.After showing us to our room, and despite being very busy with other guest, she came to greet us further by offering us a welcome to Amsterdam drink. It was the perfect start to a wonderful weekend!!

<Content>Fine family run Hotel Hotel Fita is NOT a 5 star de luxe Hotel; it is a fine small (16 bedrooms, 29 beds) hotel owned and managed by Hans and Loes de Rapper. <Author>JWBoston
<Content>A very good hotel We spent 5 nights in the Hotel Fita in Amsterdam. Both the room and the bathroom were large, one of their largest but still large by any small hotel standard, and simply but nicely furnished. The beds were comfortable. We had two twins pushed together like a king but with separate covers. I did notice that there was a real king size bed in another room. Breakfast buffet was included with the room and was pretty good, with nice pastries, eggs, bacon, cereal, fruit, juice, and coffee or tea. This is not a luxury hotel but it is comfortable. The hotel offers free phone calls within Europe and to the US (Really!) and free WIFI or use of their computer.The hosts, the de Rappers are very nice, accommodating people. They are happy to provide information and book activities and excursions, but they also told us not to waste our money on some things, like a dinner canal cruise. The location is excellent, very close to the Van Gogh Museum, Rijksmuseums and the Concertgebouw. From here it is easy to get around the city by foot, bicycle, tram and canal bus (for tourists only, but a good way to get your bearings and get to attractions).The only drawbacks were that 1) the hotel entrance is several steep steps up from the street and they do not have staff to help carry luggage (Hans deRapper helped me with my heavy bag). There is an elevator in the hotel so it's just a matter of getting your things in. 2) The bathroom has minimal toiletries with only liquid soap for both hand washing and showering/bathing. If you stay there, bring your own soap, shampoo and washcloth. The towels were adequate but there was only one hand and one bath towel each and they were not luxury linens. I'm sure that we could have gotten more if we asked, but we didn't really need them.We would certainly stay there again.

<Author>Baltimorons
<Content>Great location, great stay My husband and I stayed at Hotel Fita from 8/4 - 8/9 and never once regretted our decision. Never having visited Amsterdam, I did a lot of research before making the reservation. Hotel Fita's location was absolutely perfect for us: a half block from the Van Gogh museum, two blocks from the Rijksmuseum, and the next street parallel is full of fabulous high-end shopping, sprinkled with traditional souvenir shops, where we found everything we needed to bring home to friends and family. The hotel is also a short stroll to the Leidsplein where the real action begins! When you've had enough, wander back to Jan Luykenstraat where all is peaceful and quiet.Another reason we chose this hotel was for the included breakfast. A wonderful selection of scrambled eggs, bacon, pastries, healthy cereals, fruit and yogurt and of course, fabulous coffee to get you going for the day. During breakfast the owner and his devoted staff of really nice girls will answer any questions about the area as well as offer tips on places you might not otherwise hear about. When he found out we were planning a trip to The Hague, Hans turned us on to the Panorama Mesdag, a fascinating 360 mural of the local beachscape. Another morning one of his employees hopped on the internet to help us find our way to the local castle, Muidenslot. My husband had been working in the Netherlands the week before I joined him and was in need of fresh laundry. How convenient to have free laundry service! Face it, the rooms are traditional European style. You are not going to find jacuzzis and hot tubs in historic buildings such as Hotel Fita's. If that's what you want, stay in the suburbs. But Hotel Fita is in a great location, offers wonderful customer service, and provides a quiet, comfortable and secure place to stay. Combine that with free laundry, free internet and international phone service (my husband didn't belive me!) and a fabulous free breakfast, and you have a terrific little hotel. And if you behave yourself you get a goodie bag when you leave! How cool is that?  
<Date>Aug 16, 2007

<Author>Chris_at_large
<Content>Nice hotel in a great location This was a nice place to stay with a great hotel staff. Everyone from the owners to the women who managed the breakfast room and the front desk and did the laundry were very professional and nice. That made a big difference. We were greeted at the door by our hostess and given welcoming glasses of white wine. Very nice detail. All areas of the hotel are very clean and well maintained. The hotel offers a 20% discount on museum tickets and it is located a stone throw from the Museumplein and the Van Gogh Museum (great to visit on Friday night when it is open late) and the Rijksmuseum (also wonderful). Breakfast was served ina nice breakfast room with excellent coffee, eggs, bacon, fresh juice, cheese cold cuts, pastries, wonderful yogurt and jams and jellies, ceral, and fruit. It was the same both mornings we were there. I greatly appreciated the free laundry service (drop off a pile of dirty clothes and they are returned washed and dried to your room at the end of the day!) and the free internet terminal.A couple of things that might disappoint one in a hotel with these rates were the lack of an air conditioner in our east-facing room and that our double consisted of two twin beds pushed together. There was a very nice ceiling fan which was OK with me, but the room which was bright during the day was a bit stuffy for that reason--cool at night though. Overall, I was very happy to stay at the Fita Hotel and would recommend it to anyone. The atmosphere is very positive at this hotel and the small disappointments were more than compensated by the positives. My wife and I would happily stay there again!

<Author>sparks07
<Content>Nice Hotel but We enjoyed our stay at the Hotel Fita but perhaps were expecting too much after reading all the raving reviews. No doubt it is a great location: quiet, in a residential area and with easy access to the tram. The room we had was very basic , clean and large enough. Our room was classified as a double deluxe but are not sure about the deluxe. The two twin beds pushed together to form a double were very tiny and the side tables, attached to the headboard were right against the bed, leaving little room for error. On one side, the table is quite high and we had to place a pillow against its edge so that if you turned over and hit it, you would not injure your head or arm.  The owners are lovely people, and very friendly. If you dealt directly with them you got great service. Our bathroom did not have soap in the dispenser, the iron and the kettle did not work or perhaps it was the electrical plugs (hard to tell). Although we mentioned it to the girl on desk, these were never attended to so we used our own soap and did without an iron or kettle. We had been told that there was an iron on another floor but having to look for it was not worth it and the deluxe room is meant to have an iron in it - part of the deluxe feature, I believe. There is little flexibility here. Although we requested a certain type of room, we did not get it. This is quite understandable as it is a small hotel and very busy. However, the girl at the desk did indicate she would add a note and move us if something came available. One right next door came available later but we were not moved even though the people who took it only stayed one night. They could have put them in our room and given us our request for the last night. I guess it was too much trouble.  The breakfast was very good but perhaps not for more than two days as it is always the same. Hot foods were scrambled eggs (very good) and bacon. Then breads, cold cereal, yogurt and fruit salad. It ended at 9:30 and toward the end, things like croissants were gone so best get there early enough. The coffee was great, (freshly brewed) as was the orange juice. The atmosphere was pleasant and very friendly. I think we were spoiled by large buffet breakfasts with amazing selections that were included at our previous hotel which was about 35Euros less than Fita.  The connexxion which was recommended to us by the hotel must of had some off days as it took forever for us to get to the hotel from the airport. They got us a taxi van because the conexxion was so late. The driver took forever to get himself organized, did not seem to recognize hotel names, needed addresses to the hotels from his passengers and had to use a map to locate the hotels. Some of the passengers had been waited over an hour and this added confusion took its toll . On the return trip Conexxion was late picking us up. Although it was only about 20 - 25 minutes late, thoughts that it could be an hour made us quite anxious about getting to the airport on time. I would recommend a taxi if you have a few people as the conexxion rate is per person or the tram would be a better option. On the whole we enjoyed our stay and the owners are wonderful people - kind and friendly and we feel badly having to mention some of these points but it is important for readers to know what to expect. This is what tripadvisor is about. Keep in mind that even at these prices (160 Euro a night) this is a budget hotel. If that is what you expect, this is a great choice for you. But if you are looking for a bit more then perhaps looking further would be a good idea. I think the rooms here are all quite different and therefore the experience might be as well.  The best part of it was the owners. If this is important to you, then you will love this place. We were more interested in getting out and about and then having a nice place to relax after a day of activity and having a breakfast that would be enough to carry us through a busy day. I guess, it is true, different strokes for different folks. We enjoyed our stay but were expecting more.

<Author>shorefolk
<Content>Should be ranked as the #1 hotel in Amsterdam! We stayed at this lovely hotel in late June for a three night pre-cruise stay. We had no problems with making online reservations and several questions we had were answered quickly. We used the recommended Connexxion Airport Shuttle which deposited us at the front steps of this quaint facility.We stayed in room 32, a deluxe double room which was large by European standards and was immaculate. The room had a small balcony and overlooked an elementary school. This retired teacher loved watching the cute Dutch children arrive on various types of parent powered bikes. The community was very quiet with ATM's within a five minute walk as well as several restaurants which proved to be good. It was very close to several museums and a stop for the Canal Bus, which we rode for hours on one rainy afternoon.Hans was the perfect host who quickly fell in love with my wife's New York accent. He provided us with a fantastic breakfast each morning which was staffed by charming college students . The free telephone calls back to Maryland and the free Internet use were welcomed pluses, as well as having our laundry done for free!Our visit ended with Hans calling a private taxi for us to go to the pier.After a flawless stay, I can't see any hotel being cleaner and the staff more friendly than at the Hotel Fita.

<Content>Wonderful Hotel in a great location I stayed at Hotel Fita for two nights in late June 2007. I was traveling alone as I was working in Europe for a month and needed a break. <Author>otterco
<Content>Great service, staff, location My wife and I stayed at Hotel Fita in Amsterdam on Sat-Sun, June 9-10  was very impressed by the hotel and its staff. Check-in and check-out were very easy and quick  the two staff members I dealt with went out of their way to make sure our stay was as comfortable as possible.The breakfast was great: eggs, bacon, cereal, orange juice, coffee, cheese, pastries, bread. The included laundry service and international phone calls are definitely a plus.Hotel Fita may look a bit outside the city if you're looking on a map of Amsterdam but it is only a 5-10 minute walk (completely safe) to the Leidsplein, where things go on all the time. Plus, both the Van Gogh Museum and Reijksmuseum and Vondelpark are probably a 2-5 minute walk from the hotel.One thing I wasn't aware of, though: there is no air conditioner in the room, but that's typical of European hotels and made no difference in our stay or comfort level. Also, the room we stayed in had a ceiling fan, which was nice. The bed and sheets were clean and comfortable. The bathroom was spotless and everything worked fine--plenty of hot water and in-room facilities. Hair dryer, wireless net access, etc. Nice flat screen TV as well.One thing to note, in the interest of full disclosure (I didn't see this mentioned in other reviews): there is a school or daycare on the same block and kids run around a lot during the day (we left on a Monday morning and this was the only day we saw/heard this). Probably not an issue for tourists but if you planned to sleep late during your stay it might affect you. Just putting it out there...Take the Connexxion shuttle from Schipol -- we were dropped off second from the airport (maybe a 10-15 minute ride). The Hotel Fita staff gladly reserves your trip back in advance for you. No need for a cab.Another thing I didn't see mentioned is that there is a long street a block away from Hotel Fita that contains a lot of high-end shops, restaurants, cafes, etc. Plenty to see and do in the nice, secure, and quiet neighborhood around the hotel. This is definitely a plus, especially when you consider how crazy things get in the Leidsplein and Central Station areas in the evenings. it was nice to be in the craziness during the day and be a very short walk away to nearly total quiet at the Hotel Fita.I completely recommend Hotel Fita and would stay here again without hesitation.  
<Date>Jun 17, 2007

<Author>cedartrail
<Content>Very Nice Small Hotel This is a 16 room hotel on a quiet street in the museum district. It is run by a friendly couple, Hans and Loes de Rapper. The location is convenient for both walkers and those using public transportation. Energetic travelers with not too much luggage can get a tram (2 or 5) outside the train station and be at the hotel within about 10 minutes. Too far to walk with any luggage. The tram will deposit you within one block of the hotel (at the stop just opposite the Van Gogh museum). Taxi's are available, but pricey. Our room was up two flights of fairly steep stairs, typical of other hotels in Europe. A lift is available. The room was clean and very adequate. Not too small. Comfortable bed. The bath was modern and well equipped (hair dryer, soap dispenser, etc.) The breakfast buffet, included in the room rate, was excellent. This hotel was chosen after much research on this and other websites, both for its reasonable rate and location. We would definitely stay here again. <Author>rpnj
<Content>Average hotel. My wife and I stayed at this hotel in april 2007. We got an standard double room, and stayed there for 4 nights. It is an average hotel: 1. the location is not bad (just opposite to Van Gogh's museum, well-served by tram's lines, and about 15-20 minutes from Centraal Station by tram); 2. the staff is fine; 3. the breakfeast is okay; 4. the room was fairly clean.Overall, an average stay. <Author>SBCATraveler
<Content>Very Disappointing I am an active participant on Trip Advisor. My husband and I do quite a bit of traveling for business and pleasure and we never hesitate to rely on trip advisor's reviews. The reviews are usually accurate about the hotels we have stayed in. At the time we made our reservation at the Fita Hotel it was listed as #5 on trip advisor for hotels in Amsterdam. Unfortunately after spending four nights at the Fita, we don't share the high esteem this hotel has received.The best thing about the Fita hotel is the location. The hotel is in the museum district and one block away from the ritziest shopping street in Amsterdam. It is a quiet, convenient and safe neighborhood.Upon arriving at the Fita Hotel we were greeted by Roel, one of the workers who was very friendly and showed us our room. During the rest of our stay, we did not see anyone at the front desk, it was always deserted. It would have been nice at times to see someone at the front desk to ask some simple questions. In fact, we needed walking directions to a local restaurant to meet a friend and my husband called the number on the in-room information card. The man who answered the phone acted like he was being disturbed at 7:00pm. When my husband said to him, How are you doing? He replied, I'm tired. Not very friendly.The only time you did see any staff was at breakfast. The breakfast was adequate. Fresh squeezed orange juice, eggs, bacon, cheeses , rolls, and yogurt with fruit. Breakfast is served until 10:00am on weekends and until 9:30am on weekdays. Since we arrived on a Saturday evening all we were told by Roel breakfast was from 8:00-10:00, so on Monday morning we showed up at 9:45am and was greeted Sorry, you missed breakfast. We explained we were not told it ended at 9:30am on the weekdays, and they Sorry and we left without breakfast.The worst part about the Fita hotel was the cleanliness of the room while we were staying there. Our garbage was not emptied everyday. Along with the garbage can was broken and we told them about it and it was not fixed or replace. The worst was our soiled bed linens were not changed for three straight days. This was inexcusable  shameful and should be an embarrassement to the hotel.Overall at 140 euros a night the Fita hotel was a total disappointment. I guess you are paying for the location because you are certainly not paying for the friendliness, the food and definitely not the cleanliness of the hotel. Next time, we will choose a different hotel.

<Author>bosox2004
<Content>Liked our Hotel We spent four nights here in Oct 2006 and were given a beautiful, large corner room at the front of the building. Hans de Rapper, the owner, guided us to our room, brought us a complimentary glass of champagne, then told us about the free in-room laptop for internet access, free long distance phone service, free laundry service, and complimentary breakfast. What more could we ask for? The hotel is located on an elegant residential street a block away from the van Gogh Museum and a few steps farther to the Rijksmuseum. The breakfast downstairs includes bacon and eggs and is a more than adequate way to start the day. The only additional luxury that would be nice is air conditioning. Even though it was chilly outside during our stay, our room got warm enough to use the ceiling fan several times. The neighborhood is upscale, and there鈥檚 a supermarket, Albert Heijn, a few minutes walk away, where we picked up wine, cheese, and fruit. Leidseplein, with its plethora of restaurants and clubs, is 10-15 minutes walk away, and there are several good restaurants all around the hotel, including on the walk to Leidseplein and on the walk to and past the Concertgebuow. The tram stops about 2 blocks from the hotel for points farther away, such as the Red Light district and the Anne Frank house. We found our stay in Amsterdam to be much too short, and we intend to stay at Hotel Fita on our next visit.

<Author>MMM_Toronto
<Content>Hotel Fita is so FANTASTIC you'll never want to leave! I stayed here in Jan/Feb 2007 with my friend and our stay was fantastic!!!!! This was my first trip to Europe in a very, very long time and I couldn't be more pleased with Hotel Fita. The hotel website was great as it provided directions for how to take the Airport Shuttle or train. I ended up taking the Airport Shuttle service to the hotel and booked the round trip since it was easier. However my friend took the train (which is much cheaper) but neither of us had any problems getting to the hotel! The owners were very accomodating as I checked in quite early at around 8:30 A.M. or so! This brings me to the staff - where to begin! The staff were so friendly and gave me suggestions on the places I could visit. Hans and his wife were so friendly and made me feel a part of the family! They even reminded me that they have free laundry service which I took advantage of! I dropped my clothes off in the morning and it was in my room at the end of the day - neatly placed in a basket! In addition, my friend and I were able to make calls to Canada for free and both of us took advantage of the free internet service via the laptop which was readily available.I had read about their breakfast on the tripadvisor.com website and was certainly not disappointed! The breakfast of champions consisted of scrambled eggs, bacon, orange juice, tea/coffee, pastries, cereal, fresh fruit, etc. It was delicious and set me on my way everyday!The hotel was only a 5 - 8 mins walk from Leidsplein Square - from which you can walk to almost any tourist attractions such as the Singel Market, Amsterdam Diamond Centre, Madame Tussards, Heineken Experience, etc. The hotel was located in a residential neighbourhood which was beautiful and extremely safe. It was also a 2 min walk to the Van Gogh Museum - for which the hotel gave us discounted tickets.All in all, I loved my stay in Amsterdam and hope to come back again! That is in large part due to Hotel Fita!! I would recommend this hotel to anyone who wants to visit Amsterdam!

Quiet, yet close to museums and restaurants. My son and I walked everywhere. Can't imagine why you would need the tram. The free phone calls to the US provided my husband back home with peace of mind reports, and the free laundry enabled me to have clean PJs and jeans at the midpoint of our visit. I have never stayed in any hotel, anywhere in Europe or the US, that felt more like a home away from home.

<Author>kschm
<Content>This is where you want to stay in Amsterdam! My husband and I have just returned from Amsterdam and a six-night stay at Hotel Fita. We couldn鈥檛 have been happier with our accommodations.As was suggested to us from Hans (Fita鈥檚 very friendly owner), take the Connexxion Schiphol airport shuttle to the hotel and buy the roundtrip fare. It鈥檚 cheap, fast and no fuss. Click on the 鈥渄irections鈥?tab from Fita鈥檚 website, then on the link 鈥淐onnexxion Airport Shuttle鈥?and look at the airport map which will show you where to purchase the shuttle tickets and then where to catch the van outside. We didn鈥檛 have to wait at all ~ plenty of shuttles available. And on our return, no fuss in the AM 鈥?24 hours prior to departure, ask the Fita staff to call to reserve your spot back to Schiphol. And so about the 鈥渟taff鈥濃€︹€?Hans and his wife were on holiday for most of our stay in Amsterdam. This was unfortunate because, as we found out on our last night there, he is a wealth of knowledge and a generally fun person to chat with. The employee鈥檚 that were there for our stay did a great job in their absence. Breakfast was served each morning from 8-9:30 and was delicious. Fresh squeezed orange juice, individual pots of coffee for each table, scrambled eggs, bacon, meats, cheeses, pastries, cold cereal, yogurt, fruit鈥?.we left each morning 鈥渇ueled up鈥?for the day.Our room was a double medium and was comfortable in size. Our beds were two twins pushed together which worked very well for my husband and I who are both over six feet tall. The room was large enough for a little table and two chairs. The bathroom was huge and had a great full powered hairdryer, dispensers for cups and soap, large tub/shower combo and nice size sink counter area. We really liked the soap and cup dispensers ~ nothing worse than those itty bitty bars of soap that slip and slide their way onto the floor and no worry that the glassware has leftover lipstick or baked on crusty stuff. The room also had an electric pot to make almost instant boiling water for espresso, hot chocolate and other choices for in room hot drinks. And clean, clean, clean. I was most impressed with how impeccably clean the place is. It鈥檚 a totally non-smoking facility which is quite nice. For non-smokers, there is no worry of smoke seeping in from other rooms or hallways and no nicotine residue on the walls, linens or woodwork. The free internet and long distance was a really nice and comforting touch.The Hotel is located in a quaint little neighborhood that is away from the bustling nightlife. It鈥檚 the best of both worlds really because it鈥檚 only a short walk or tram ride to Leidseplein or Spui for loads of activity. And you couldn鈥檛 be closer to the museums and concert hall (Concertgebouw). I鈥檝e read a couple negative posts regarding the steepness of the stairs. Yes, the stairs are steep, but you鈥檙e in Amsterdam!! This Hotel (which Hans has completely renovated) was built in 1902 and steep stairs are typical for any structure in this city of this age. The Hotel has an elevator to take you to upper floors if the stairs pose a problem. We learned to be careful managing all staircases while touring the city.I took photos of the hotel to post here but they didn't turn out. I have taken another look at Fita's website and feel that all of their pictures are very representative of the accomodations. Check it out if you haven't already.Be sure to look at the schedule for the Concertgebouw and get tickets in advance (Fita will arrange) for any concerts you might want to attend. They have free lunch time concerts (30 minutes in length) on Wednesdays. Get there on the early side as they fill up. We bought the annual museum card (available at any museum) and found it to be a good value since we visited both the Rijks and Van Gogh three times. Do your research in advance and check out the other museums on the card 鈥?we would recommend Het Rembrandthuis, Museum van Loon, Museum Willet-Holthuysen and Museum Amsterlkring. You must take a quick tour through the red light district 鈥?this is where Museum Amsterlking is located. And while there, check out Oude Kerk (鈥淥ld Church鈥? Anne Frank Huis is not on included on the annual museum card but worth the little they charge. Hotel Fita gives a discount coupon for a canal ride which we enjoyed. Go around dusk so that you can enjoy the city from the water while there is still a little daylight but also as the buildings and bridges light up. And although it may sound hokey, do the Heineken Experience. It was a blast!! Page down on the reviews here and look at the post for the special hand sign which will get you a free long neck to enjoy at the end.So, if you鈥檙e planning a trip to Amsterdam, look no further for accommodations  Hotel Fita is the best value for your money and we consider it our Amsterdam 鈥渉ome away from home鈥?

<Author>RetiredTravelers
<Content>Measured up to the reviews My wife and I spent three nights in Amsterdam. We had intended to stay at a canal hotel, but all of the highly-rated ones were booked up by the time I made a reservation (about three weeks in advance of the stay). Based on TripAdvisor reviews, I then called the Hotel Fita and was successful in booking a room. The location turned out to be much better than I had anticipated; two major museums are 1-3 blocks away, and the city's other major sights are easily accessible by foot or trolley. The hotel itself is on a quiet street. As others have noted, the only significant drawback is the steep stairs from the street to the lobby.In general our experience reflects those of most other reviewers. The room--a double Medium, in the hotel's classification system--was clean, well-appointed, comfortable, and quite adequate in size. The proprietor provided excellent recommendations for restaurants, tours, etc. The breakfast is indeed quite good. All in all, a most pleasant stay; I would have no hesitation to stay there again in the future.

<Author>Vallane
<Content>Adored Hotel Fita We took our first trip to Europe in May 2006. Our last stop was 2 nights in Amsterdam. We booked the Hotel Fita based in large part on Trip Advisor reviews. When we arrived we were buzzed in by Hans, who turned out to be the owner along with his wife Lus. After several minutes of pleasant conversation we were shown to our room. It was gorgeous, large with a balcony and the largest bathroom we encountered during our eight nights in Europe. As we were getting settled in there was a knock on the door and there was Hans with a bowl of peanuts and champagne. As he suggested we stood on our balcony and toasted to our first night in Amsterdam.The location is great, near the museums, in a primarily residential neighborhood. Only 1 block away you can hop on a tram or bus. Restaurants and nightlife are within a 10 minute walk. Breakfast was wonderful, and as we were told, just follow your nose downstairs in the morning. We particularly loved the fresh squeezed orange juice, eggs and bacon. We were offered discounted tickets to the museums at breakfast. Exceptional service.Two nights were not nearly enough to see Amsterdam and enjoy the Hotel Fita.

<Author>ArtandArtHistoryProf
<Content>A Squeaky Clean Gem! Great for families w/ kids...playyard closeby. This is the hotel we loved the most on our 2 week trip in Europe in March of 2006. There were three of us, husband, child (6) and me in the room...it was so clean and neat - the bed was very comfy and the bedding was all white, fluffy cottons...(no synthetic fabrics). The view was so nice....we had a top floor room with a small balcony overlooking the street and it was enjoyable to be in such a family neighborhood tucked inbetween Amsterdaam's Fifth Avenue and the two major Art Museums. It is katty-corner form a public school built in 1900 called the Neue School--the kids played outside at the playyard across from the hotel with thier teachers and it was nice to hear them playing. Also, nice to have a little playyard form my son to play in too...We traveled there to attend the festivities and art shows celebrating 400th year celebration of Rembrandt's birth. I am an Art Professor in the Midwest and have travelled to Europe 3 x now and I always love to find hotels this friendly, CLEAN (have I mentioned that?) and located well. As customary in Europe, the rooms are small to us Americans but the windows were like 12 feet high so it seemed light and airy.If you are looking for a hotel like this with a grocery store around the corner (underground), major park, great shopping, museums, bakery, and awesome public transportaion within footsteps- THIS IS IT!!! I am a very picky traveller on a low/mid-range budget...too bad I won't be reviewing my Paris hotels this favorably - We will stay there again...for sure...but not in March--it is too windy and cold there that time of year !!!! I should add that the staff cheerfully did a load of laundry for us and it came back immaculate that afternoon. We left the staff nice tips...they earned it!

<Author>janetc20
<Content>I thought it was lovely I stayed at the Hotel Fita for 12 nights and had very few problems. We arrived very early in the morning (much earlier than we thought we would) so we woke up Hans at 7am on a Sunday morning in order to stow our luggage in the lobby until we could check in. He was a little cranky, but who wouldn't have been???? He had the staff give us coffee in the breakfast room and told us a few places in the neighborhood to go until we could check in -- since, of course, the people who were checking out of our scheduled room were still sleeping! Not a great situation when jetlagged but definitely not the hotel's fault. In fact, when we checked in, the front desk staff offered to explain the city layout and provide other information. We were too tired to hear it then and never got around to it but... they did bring a welcome beverage to our room, which was a nice touch. Next time, I'll time my flight arrival more sanely! In order to accomodate our long stay during a very busy time, we were scheduled to change rooms twice and we did. So we stayed in a standard, medium, and deluxe room. All were as advertised on the website, very clean and plenty spacious. Each time we changed rooms, we just did a rough pack and the staff moved our things. On the appointed day, the staff brought us our new room keys while we were at breakfast, explained the procedure, and it was all taken care of by the time we came back from the day's adventure to freshen up for dinner. No problems at all.We were there during a rather unexpected hot spell and there is not much in the way of climate control (well, anywhere in Amsterdam -- I think the locals were as surprised as we were) but sleeping with the windows open wasn't a problem and was mostly comfortable. The beds themselves were very comfortable and the pillows were good (two per person which I thought was plenty). The bathrooms, as I mentioned, were surprisingly spacious and clean and the showers had good water pressure and plenty of hot water. The breakfasts were good and filling with the lovely fresh squeezed orange juice and plenty of coffee. The staff in the breakfast room were very accomodating. I had an unfortunate personal situation occur during my stay and the owners and staff were as accomodating as possible and definitely (and apparently genuinely) interested in my well-being. I would not hesitate to recommend the Hotel Fita to other travelers -- in fact, I already told one of my very good friends to stay there when she travels to Amsterdam on business in October! Enjoy the Hotel Fita....I will stay there again if my travels ever take me to Amsterdam again.  
<Date>Jul 11, 2006

<Author>Wandering-Around
<Content>A Pleasant Stay at the Fita We stayed at the Fita for 4 nights in late June, 2006. We were greeted with a snack and a drink upon arrival. Our room was large, with ceiling fan and small TV. The hotel is nice and extremely clean, and the innkeepers were very pleasant and helpful. Breakfast is included and is very nice.We found the combination of location, price, free wi-fi, free calls to the US, and laundry service to be wonderful on our vacation. There are, however, some quirks that you need to be aware of: - The Fita is a small hotel, and the lift is so small that 2 people are quite cozy when riding in it. - The front desk is not regularly staffed. This did not pose a problem, as you can always dial the innkeepers, and you can be buzzed in at the front door.- A double room is commonly two twin beds pushed together. This is quite common in Europe, so be prepared. If you need a double bed or queen bed in your hotel, make sure that you are specific in your request.- The sheets were a bit rough and industrial feeling.- There is a kindergarten / primary school next door, and the children play outside. This can generate quite a bit of noise during the daytime.If you are expecting a cozy, comfortable, clean hotel, then the Hotel Fita is a great place to stay. If you are expecting an Americanized version of the Hilton - Fita is not for you.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Super friendly Fita I stayed at the Fita 22-25 June with my wife and young daughters (7 and 4) and my elderly parents.Everything about the hotel was truly excellent. It is exactly as described - a small family- run spotlessly clean hotel. The small 2 person lift was just what was needed for my mother who has a dodgy knee.We had booked two double rooms and separate single beds had been set up in one of the rooms advance for the childrenHans and Loes (the owners) are indeed very friendly and helpful - our daughters loved the attention (and little gifts).Breakfast comprises the usual hot drink choices, eggs (scrambled and boiled), bacon, bread rolls, home-made jams toast, pastries, cereals cheeses and (a favourite for the children) chocolate milk- all that you'd need.You need to arrive before 10.30pm on arrival but once you are checked in, you get a key card for the outside door and you can then came and go as you please.We had an early flight on our day of departure and although it was before breakfast was due, the staff made sure we had bread cereal toast and juice and coffee and that a taxi for 6 to turn up right on time. We arranged to check out the night before which was no trouble. For a family trip, it was in an ideal location - in the quiet museum quarter - only yards from the Van Gogh museum and the posh designer shops and a small walk to lots of restaurants and the tram stops to get into the centre.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Disappointed with Fita We reserved a 'double' deluxe room on line for three nights hoping that we would recieve comfortable accommodation close to the centre at reasonable rates to spend an enjoyable time for a birthday trip. The booking was trouble free and response was good and the price was acceptable at 150euros per night. On arrival, we had to wait at the door to be let in and given a reasonably warm welcome and first impressions were that the hotel was ok. After check in, we were shown to our room after a short journey in a very small lift and on entering the room, we had an instant feeling of disappointment. Although the room was large and airy, there were two single beds pushed together (not what we expected or explained on the web site) and we found the room to be 'grubby' with a strong smell of disenfectant coming from the bathroom. I phoned the owner from the room to ask for a room with a double bed and was told that I had not booked one, furthermore, he was very offensive when I expressed my disappointment at the quality and suggested that we leave immediately (10.30p.m!) He made no attempt to help our situation, leaving us to find alternative accommodation for the following day; this meant enquiring at other hotels in the area that evening to arrange something more suitable for the remainder of our stay. Thankfully, we were successful and left the following morning, checking into a very high standard, professional hotel. On leaving Hotel Fita, we were subject to a very abrupt and cold experience and were glad to leave. The propietors of Hotel Fita need to revisit their website to amend their description of the accommodation offered, as we found it to be very misleading as to what the standard of this 'hotel' actually is, or, upgrade their rooms to meet their advertisment. Overall, I certainly would not recommend this 'hotel'.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great fit at the Fita When we arranged to visit Amsterdam, we chose not to stay at a trendy, canal side hotel, but at the less expensive hotel Fita in the museum district. The Fita also offered such perks as a full breakfast, free laundry and free phone calls to the USA and to Europe.The hotel had a lift which was welcome, since I have a bad knee, and the spotlessly clean room had a large bathroom with ample counter space.Loes de Rapper was helpful in proving information on getting around Amsterdam. She sold us discoount tickets to the museums, which saved us from waiting on long lines to get in.In the neighborhood--and it was very much a neighborhood-- were a number of good restaurants within walking distance, as were the canals and Vondel Park, an oasis of greenery, peppered with lakes and streams.The Fita felt like home for the eleven days that we stayed there. We would heartily recommend the Hotel Fita to any friends traveling to Amsterdam.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A fabulous hotel in the Museum District I was recently in Amsterdam and stayed at the Hotel Fita. It is on a quiet street right in the heart of the Museum District, so it is very close to both the Rijksmuseum and the Van Gogh museum. This hotel is extremely clean and well tended, and the hosts (the de Rapper family) are friendly and always very helpful. I spent 12 nights at this hotel and staying there greatly contributed to my enjoyment of Amsterdam and Holland.

<Content>Museumplein Hotel Fita is a great place, nestled in a leafy street, just behind the art museums. If you want to keep away from all the noise of the but be near all the life of Amsterdam, this is the place to be. Fita is also close to the trams so you can get around easily, but we prefered to walk as everything is so close.  Very Clean, very friendly and just big enough. We are not keen on the big hotels where they are so impersonal.Amsterdam is going through a massive clean up and is attracting more sober visitors so we enjoyed it. We visited mainly for the art exhibition but found plenty of time to see other things. The Willet Museum was great, it gave you a good idea of how life was and the Rembrandt Museum has been improved dramatically.Fita are happy to recommend restaurants and it is worth taking their advice, every one has been a winner!We will not go to any other hotel when we visit Amsterdam..................Carole Tom Margaret David

<Author>axle99
<Content>Weekend Break We travelled in a group of 12 for a suprise 60th birthday. Our group ranged in age from twenty somethings to sixty somethings.The hotel is located in a quiet area outside the city centre, close to the Van Gogh Museum. The rooms were large,comfortable and clean which are the key ingredients for a stay away from home. Steps are steep but this appears to be a feature of most properties in Amsterdam and a lift is available. All of Amsterdam can be reached on foot and we were happy to have found a hotel in a quiet location outside the centre. Accomodation in Amsterdam is quiet expensive. As a small family run hotel, the Fita Hotel offers good value for money (in comparison to some of the bigger name hotels we reviewed online) and we would happily stay there again on a return trip to Amsterdam.

I would stay at this hotel again because it was in a quiet area and it felt safe.ps the stairs would give you the head staggers!
