<Author>Glasgow_Member06
<Content>Excellent base to explore Amsterdam Just returned from 3 nights at the Hotel Fita. Good, clean basic hotel. Very warm welcome from our hosts, Mr  Mrs de Rapper. Good breakfasts with bacon and eggs if you like something hot. The hotel is very well situated - close to the main museums and concert hall and within a two-minute walk to the Number 2 and 5 trams which take you to the main station and the city centre tourist areas. Mrs de Rapper recommended some local restaurants that turned out to be real finds - excellent food at inexpensive prices. Some reviewers complain about the noise from the kids at the nearby school. Forget it; it's not a problem. My wife and I would have no hesitation in recommending the Fita. You'll find it hard to get such a warm welcome elsewhere.

<Author>Virginia19
<Content>A Pleasant Stay in Amsterdam We had a very pleasant stay at the Hotel Fita. We stayed in Room 24, which I think is one of the bigger rooms in the hotel. It was definitely much bigger than the room we had in Paris. The room was very clean and well kept, and while the decor was nothing special, it was fine for our purposes. The double bed was really two single beds pushed together but they were comfortable and we had no problem.The bathroom was very clean and soap was provided but not shampoo or conditioner. The room overlooked the street, but we were not bothered by noise at all. The street is very pretty, tree lined, and quiet just about all the time. While we did hear some noise from the schoolyard in the afternoon, we generally were not there very long in the afternoon so it was no big deal for us.The breakfast is included in the room cost. I would say the breakfast is good but nothing outstanding. The fresh squeezed orange juice is delicious, as is the fruit salad and the yogurt. The eggs and bread and are OK, but the bread seemed not quite fresh. However, having breakfast there is a quick way to get the day started and we had no real complaints at all.The DeRapper family, which runs the hotel, was very helpful and accommodating. We hardly saw Hans, but spoke to Loes on a number of occasions and she was always pleasant and helpful. Often there is no one at the front desk but you can easily contact someone by calling 144 from your room.Having free phone calls to the US and internet access was great. We borrowed their laptop for a whole day to check on emails, and it worked out very well. Even though we offered to bring it back several times, they said we could keep it until another guest requested it.We found the location of the hotel very convenient. If you are interested in museums, this is the place to be! For other activities, it is about a 15 minute walk to the Anne Frank House, and about a 20-25 minute walk to Center City. For the Anne Frank House try to go either first thing or later in the afternoon to beat the crowd.The number 2 or 5 trams pass very close to the Hotel and work well on those days when you just don't feel like walking anymore. We arrived in Amsterdam by train and took a taxi to the Hotel (15 Euros), but I think we could have easily done the trip by tram at much less cost.We took a taxi to the airport when leaving, which Loes arranged for us, and it was 30 Euros. It only took about 20 minutes, but it was a Saturday morning.All in all it was a wonderful stay. If we go back to Amsterdam, and I hope we do, we will definitely stay at the Hotel Fita!  
<Date>Oct 23, 2005

<Author>nikatknight
<Content>Very Nice Hotel We recently spent 5 nights at the Hotel Fita while in Amsterdam. The location was good, one block from the Van Gogh Museum. Our rate included free museum passes and free telephone calls to the US. The breakfasts were very good and included eggs, bacon, breads, cheese, etc. The only drawback was our downstairs room. I would have preferred a room on one of the upper floors as opposed to being on the ground floor as the school next door had many kids playing, during recess, right outside of the window. It wasn't a big deal for us as we were gone right after breakfast, but if you sleep in it could be an annoyance. All in all, I liked the hotel and would definitely stay there again.

<Author>Mary_Barry
<Content>Hotel Fita: Dutch Treat Just spent 2 nights at Hotel Fita at the tail end of a 3-week trip to France and Holland. Hotel Fita was by far the best value of our travel accommodations. The room (#26) was not by any means romantic - more like a very upscale dorm room - but it was reasonably sized and extremely clean. (Cleanliness appears to be somewhat of a fetish with the owners, but heck, you could experience far less wholesome fetishes, especially in Amsterdam!) This particular room had lots of windows and a balcony, which was nice. It also had amenities such as a safe, a reading light on each side of the bed, and a full-sized bathtub with - hoorah - a real shower and complete shower curtain! Beds were two singles pushed together, but each had two comfy pillows and the sheets had been washed and ironed into a state of sublime crispness. We never met Mr. and Mrs. de Rapper, the owners, but the young staff members who we did talk with were most helpful. The staff is sort of invisible most of the time, but appear when you call them, which is fine. The neighborhood is first-rate, quiet and nice for walking. The Rijksmuseum is less than 5 minutes walk away, and is worth visiting even though much of it is closed for renovation. The part that's open is excellent. Vondel Park, also very close, was a disappointment; the little ponds were full of bottles, beercans and all kinds of unsavory litter. Ac tually, much of Amsterdam was disappearing under a layer of trash and graffitti; too bad that such an interesting, cosmopolitan city appears so little cared-for by residents and visitors.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>An average stay Whilst glad of this hotel over some of the others seen in Amsterdam, the hotel we encountered was somewhat different to the majority of reviews read here on tripadvisor. It was easy to get to and from the hotel and airport, the shuttle leaves you to either door and the price was very reasonable. The hotel was conveniently located, being very close to the Van Gogh and Rijksmuseum. It was a nice area, a street up from some fancy shops (Chanel, Gucci, etc). The short walk into the centre of Amsterdam was pleasant, so no use of public transport was needed.Our room, number 12, was of reasonable size and was comfortable and functional. It did lack character, and the bathroom could be seen as a little clinical, but at least it was all kept very clean. The double bed consisted of two singles pushed together, which whilst expected is always a little disappointing. Still, they were comfortable with plenty of pillows, which most other hotels lack. The ceiling fan was a welcome addition.Breakfast was poor. The scrambled eggs were in need of some scrambling, forming a huge omelette in their dish. The pastries were plain-tasting, and cereal lacked crunch. Milk clotted up on contact with the coffee. My girlfriend and I recommend visiting one of the patisseries down past Leidesplein where they have good coffee for little over a euro, and a huge range of delicious pastries. Many shops sell fruit, more types than you could name, and these are also good for picking up a very fresh breakfast.The de Rappers were not all they were cracked up to be. We only saw Loes once the whole stay, and Hans on the occasions we did see him was loud and standoffish. This didn鈥檛 pose a problem, just is contradictory to the reports we read here prior to our visit. Having said this, Loes giving us our bearings at the start was appreciated, as it鈥檚 always nice to have an idea where to start off in a new city.Without meaning to sound like I'm complaining, one day our room was not cleaned or our towels changed. This posed no real problem, but does underline the overall service as nothing special.Worth noting for those light sleepers out there is that the curtains were paper thin, and so it was never really 鈥榙ark鈥?in the room.Tripadvisor left me with high expectations, but realistically the hotel was everything it should have been. All in all it was a pleasant stay and a pleasant hotel. I would recommend the hotel to others, I just don鈥檛 see what all the fuss was about myself!

<Author>PeachfromGA
<Content>Perfect Hotel A friend and I just completed a 5-night stay at the Hotel Fita, and it was the perfect ending to our vacation. The room rate was reasonable when compared what was being charged at other hotels in the city. The hotel is spotless; the breakfast plentiful; and above all the staff super friendly and helpful. Its small size allows each guest to receive personal attending. The location is outstanding. We felt very safe walking around the area at all times. It's just a short block from the VanGogh Museum and Rijksmuseum. Included in the price were a choice of entry tickets to either of these museums. (Don't miss them; they are extraordinary!) Also received a discount on the room rate for an extended stay - more than 3 nights.Trams heading to all the sights in the city are only one block away. I heartily recommend the Hotel Fita to anyone looking for a warm and friendly hotel in Amsterdam.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great family hotel in very good location I totally agree with everything said in the previous review titled Comfortable Hotel. We stayed in one of the larger rooms that was spotlessly clean with a very nice size bathroom. The staff were very friendly and helpful and tried to answer all the queries we had.The hotel location couldn't be better as it is only one block away from the Van Gogh and Rijksmuseums. It is also within a 10 minute walk to Leidesplein and then a nice stroll into the centre. Alternatively, the trams are easy to use and both the number 2 and 5 go into the centre.If you have some free time take the opportunity to walk the few blocks from the hotel to the Vondelpark which is a very large green park with several streams and ponds. On the evening we went there it seemed that most of Amsterdam was having a picnic on the grass or listening to a free open-air concert.We would definitely recommend this hotel to anyone wanting a good, clean, friendly hotel in a convenient location. We will be going back again soon.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Good Choice I would recommend the Hotel Fita as a good choice for a quiet, clean, well-located hotel in Amsterdam. It is two minutes walk to the Van Gogh museum (a must-see sight), and about 20 minutes walk to Anne Frank House (another must-see sight). It is located on the edge of the central core, and everything in the central core is within a 30-minute walk or a short tram ride.We stayed in a deluxe room for 130 euros a night, which was located on the highest floor at the back/side of the hotel (fortunately, there is an elevator!). The room was a comfortable size, with large windows looking onto a pedestrian street, and was surprisingly quiet. It also includes a small safe, which was a nice touch.The breakfast was quite substantial -- pastries, cereal, yogurt, fruit, eggs, and bacon (or some similar type of meat, which I didn't try which is why I can't remember exactly what it was). The owner is very hospitable and helpful.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Fantastic Fita! We recently spent ten days at the Hotel Fita in Amsterdam. The Fita's location is absolutely perfect - very easy walking access to the museums and Leidesplein (area with multiple restaurants/pubs), and steps away from the tram stop. It is in a quiet residential area, with great shopping very close as well. We stayed over the Queen's birthday, which is a major national holiday in the Netherlands, and it was delightful. We could easily get into the action, yet have a quiet place to rest at night. The room was immaculate with all the ammenities you could possibly need. There was no excessive noise, and I'm a light sleeper. The staff was wonderful in all regards. The buffet breakfast was consistently delicious, fresh, and served in a sparkling environment. Fresh squeezed orange juice and excellent coffee, too! Now let's talk about Hans, the proprietor..... Hello, Hans! This gentleman has given new meaning to the word character. We even dragged him out of his abode one evening to help us figure out how to rescue a trapped cat in the building next door. And his carpentry skills...you must check out room 36. What a guy! Seriously, both he and his lovely wife are exceptional hosts, and they operate the highest quality establishment. To consider staying anywhere else in Amsterdam would be a waste of your time and money.

<Author>Lexicles
<Content>Comfortable Hotel My daughter and I recently stayed at the Fita. We were in a standard room that, whilst small, certainly met all of our needs. It was very clean, the bed was comfortable, pillows good and we had a clean, large bathroom. Lots of nice little touches, for example we had a chocolate on our pillow on arrival, there is a little inflatable duck in the bathroom, and when we left we were given a fridge magnet of the hotel.My daughter loved the breakfast - freshly squeezed orange juice included. It isn't a huge selection, but what there is is top quality and very fresh.The hotel is in a very good location, close to the Van Gogh and Rijksmuseum - this is especially important when you have a child with you as there are some places that you would rather not be near at night! We had no problem finding some good restaurants, including a combined Argentinian steak house/Italian restaurant just around the corner. The next street along seemed to be Amsterdams answer to Bond Street - Lacoste, Chanel etc which was nice to browse. We used the trams (get a strippenkaart at the station or the Albert Heijn supermarket round the corner from the hotel). Trams 2 and 5 stop outside the Van Gogh museum which is steps away from the hotel. Don't walk from the station - it's quite a long way with luggage. We would definitely recommend this hotel. Don't go if you want big hotel style and luxury, but if you want good value, clean accommodation and some nice extras (we got half price Van Gogh museum tickets) - then head straight there.  
<Date>May 19, 2005

<Author>Galloping
<Content>Not a good Fita for us I booked Hotel Fita based purely on the reviews from the Tripadvisor website which depicted the hotel as a charming, friendly place in a quiet location away from the excesses of the city.The Museum area is very quiet relative to everywhere else and although it is slightly outside the main spots, the trams are excellent and so there is no bother getting to and from the livelier city. So in this respect the location was fine.However in terms of charm, the Hotel Fita has little. The decor is dull. The hotel had false ceilings in all the rooms I was in, making it extremely clinical. Our room once had a high old ceiling but a suspended one was put in, totally hanging in mid air where it couldn't match up to the wall because of the lovely long windows. Lighting was by flourescent tubes hidden above the curtains that buzzed for the entire time they were on. Other lighting was only provided by two bedside lamps, completely insufficient so the buzzing had to be tolerated. We stayed in a double de luxe room. Double....well there were 2 single beds pushed together. Clean.....the room was very clean as was the bathroom. The bathroom was a fine size with a good vanity area. Good lighting, which can so often be a problem in hotels. So this was very positive. However the bathroom was let down by all the awful dispensers on the walls. One for hand soap, toilet paper, shower gel, plastic cups. It all felt very similar to being in the toilet facilities at a school or shopping centre. Do that many people pack the rolls of loo paper away with them before they leave that this was necessary? More disposables in the main room, cups for the coffee tray were plastic with a good supply of plastic inserts if you required. After a long day on my feet between the museums and the shopping I would just have liked to have my coffee from a cup.Finally, the management boast that they know there guests by name. Well I think they would find it difficult to know ours as we never met them. On the morning we were leaving I looked up the phone numbers they had left in the room so that I could call someone to arrange a taxi. There was no number for reception, only the management, so I called that. I was greeted by a most unfriendly host who quite literally scolded me on the phone for making the call and then did so much heavy breathing to reiterate how irritated he was I did begin to wonder who was the guest and where was the lovely man who everyone speaks of on this site ? We eventually got a taxi by leaving our room and going down two flights of stairs to the breakfast room to find a staff member to call one for us. By the time we left that morning I was so annoyed, I almost felt I had been robbed as I signed for the bill. If you like the smell of bleach to assure you that a hotel room has been cleaned, by all means stay at the Hotel Fita. If you are looking for charm, then this is certainly not the place. Breakfast is not so fantastic that you wouldn't get the same elsewhere, and given that we had to send back sour milk on our first morning, I am not so sure that this place is as efficient as they would like you to believe. Its clean.....thats about it. I am at a complete loss as to know where all the fantastic reviews on this site come from.  
<Date>Dec 13, 2004

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Unforgettable Hotel Fita, from Spain Thanks to our election of the Hotel Fita, our stay in Amsterdam was unforgettable.We are used to traveling, but it is not easy to find hotels where the stay is so pleasant; even less, in tourist destinations so important as Amsterdam. Moreover, when traveling with a 6 years-old boy, we really appreciate the characteristics that make easy the satisfaction of our neceessities is this matter.And in this way, they are several reasons that made the stay at the Hotel Fita so extraordinary:1. The localization: the beautiful building of beginning of the 20 century (built to the typical style of Amsterdam), wich is just barely at 50 meters from the Van Gogh Museum and, therefore, also beside the Rijskmuseum and the Stedelijk Museum. The pleasant walk to the Leidseplein Square (one of the most lively night spaces, where there are plenty of restaurants and terraces; and very calm for families) it is carried out in just 5 minutes. Also in 5 minutes you can arrive to the romantic Vondelpark that also has an area for child games. For other locations, there is a complete service of trams, wich bring you to the most tourist places.2. Services: the Hotel Fita overcomes the requeriments of tranquility, cleaning and health; with an exquisite politic of no smokers.3. Welcome: staying at the Hotel Fita, you will realize that the family de Rapper really enjoys their lifestyle, beyond their work. The warmth with which they welcome you, the constant concern with which they worry about your satisfaction, and the atmosphere of familiarity among their employees, all toghether, makes that you really notice a true custom attention. 4. Details: family de Rapper is specially generous in excepctional details. For example: they give 2 tickets for the Van Gogh Museum or for the Rijksmuseum (at your election) and they offer you others tickets (without any additional cost), so you don't need to spend your time queuing up for any tickets. They are pleased to carry out personal favors as bringing you, in their own automobile, to a Rent-a-car company, or to make an urgent laundry for the boy's clothes (and for free), etc.5. Tourist information: the information of cultural events, what you shouldn't miss in Amsterdam and in the rest of the country, is really attractive and, mainly, far away from the sequential information that you get at the receptions of other hotels and, also, in the overcrowded offices of tourism. Trusting their advices is a guarantee os satisfaction.Lastly, you can make yourself understand with them in all languages, also in a friendly spanish, learned in long stays in our coasts.

<Content>Special time in a wonderful city!!!! Our stay at the Hotel Fita was a very special time in a wonderful city. We were completing our vacation after visiting Italy, Belgium, and Maastricht. We were greeted by our enthusiastic host, Hans, who described many interesting things about the city. The hotel was just incredible. The premises was sparkling clean, from the main entrance to the rooms. The double deluxe was spacious and included a large spotless bathroom. Do yourself a favor and invite Hans to join you for a cup. The free telephone calls to the United States and Europe were an added bonus. The Van Gogh and Rijks museums were steps away. Great shopping and restaurants were also close by. When we return to Amsterdam we will definitely stay with Hans and Loes de Rapper again at the Hotel Fita.
